The existing single-target action types (destroy_creature etc.) are **UNTOUCHED**, so their behaviour/tests are unaffected (no regression surface). **Builder `build_stack_payload_multi_creature_simple`** validates `kind` in the removal set + that EVERY id is a legal creature via the SAME `creature_target_controller_ok` gate the single-target builders use (targets locked at cast, MTG-correct); rejects empty set. **Handler `handle_multi_creature_effect`** loops `apply_creature_effect(kind, id)` â€” which already no-ops a target that left the battlefield, so a partially-illegal set still resolves for the legal ones (rule 608.2b/c), verified by MT4. **GOTCHA (bug-235):** a new castable action_type needs adding to the `game_stack_items_action_type_check` CHECK (last redefined mig 107) â€” registering the handler/builder is not enough; the INSERT fails otherwise. mig 112 reproduces that allow-list + 1. **Authoring:** removal effects gained optional `targets?: number` (Zod + LLM); `targets > 1` â†’ multi. NOT a new form field (the guided form's single creature picker covers single-target; multi is JSON/AI-authorable for now). **Client:** `castMultiCreatureEffect` wrapper; `getSpellPlan` detects `targets > 1` on a removal effect â†’ a new `multi_creature` plan; a multi-select picker (toggle creatures, capped at count, confirm) wired through `onMultiCreatureEffect`, modelled on the creature_effect/fight pickers. **Test gotcha (bug-236):** the harness runs one tx per test, so an expected-raise poisons it â€” a rejection test (MT5/MT6) must not run post-assertion queries. Tests MT1 (destroy two), MT2 (tap two), MT3 (bounce two), MT4 (partial fizzle), MT5 (illegal target rejects cast), MT6 (empty rejects) â€” cast via put_action_on_stack directly, **zero new fixtures**. 259/259, tsc/lint clean. **Remaining targeting reach: non-creature permanents + player-target triggers (the other two slices), and divided damage.**

- [2026-06-05] **Tier-3 `search_library` variants (migration 111) â€” graveyard dest, battlefield-tapped, name filter, reveal metadata.** Four backward-compatible additions to the existing tutor (every new field optional; defaults preserve current behaviour), all confined to the two `search_library` branches of the reproduced `apply_trigger_effects` + `submit_decision` (mig 110 base): **(1) `to:'graveyard'`** (Entomb/Buried Alive) â€” a 4th destination branch in the submit apply loop, mirroring the choose_cards generic `zone=v_dest` move. **(2) `tapped:true`** (Rampant Growth/fetchlands) â€” carried in params; the battlefield branch reads `is_tapped = coalesce((params->>'tapped')::boolean,false)` (was hardcoded false). **(3) `filter.name`** â€” the options query gains `and (v_name is null or c.name ilike '%'||v_name||'%')` alongside the existing type_line match; prompt appends "named X". **(4) `reveal:true`** â€” NO real sink exists in this engine ("reveal" everywhere else just means "the option set shown for a decision", never recorded state; there's `is_face_down` but no `is_revealed`, no game-log table). Implemented as the honest minimal sink: stamp the found ids into `result.revealed` via `update ... returning * into v_decision` (so the row returned to the caller carries it) â€” auditable METADATA only, no opponent-facing UI broadcast. **Authoring split (the key call):** `graveyard` went into the guided form (clean enum addition to SEARCH_DESTINATIONS â€” no breakage); **`tapped`/`reveal`/`filter.name` are JSON/AI-only** (Zod + LLM, NOT the registry), matching the gain_control untap/haste precedent. **Why name stayed out of the form (bug-230):** adding a `name` sub-field to the registry filter OBJECT broke 5 builder characterization tests â€” `parseFields` rejects a filter carrying only type_line (non-optional sub-field absent â†’ JSON mode), and `fieldToJson` emits EVERY object sub-field with no empty-drop, so `name:''` would leak into every serialized tutor. The object-field machinery has no "optional sub-field that drops when empty" support; rather than deepen it, name is JSON/AI-authorable like the other extras. Zod: `to` enum += 'graveyard', added `tapped`/`reveal` booleans + `filter.name`. Tests SLG1 (graveyard), SLT1 (tapped)/SLT2 (default untapped guard), SLN1 (name filter narrows options), SLR1 (reveal records ids)/SLR2 (no reveal â†’ no key) â€” all via `castSpellEffect`, **zero new fixtures**. 253/253, tsc/lint clean. **Remaining Tier-3 frontier: targeting reach (player/permanent/multi-target).**

- [2026-06-05] **Multi-opponent edict `sacrifice who:'each_opponent'` (migration 110) â€” sequential decision CHAIN, the deferred mig-108 follow-up.** "Each opponent sacrifices a creature" (Plaguecrafter): every opponent chooses their OWN creature, so it's N sequential decisions that must all finish before the program resumes. **Mechanism â€” NO new decision_type (reuses 'sacrifice'), no stack changes:** the parked decision's `params` now carries the remaining-opponent QUEUE (`edict_queue`, jsonb array of player-id strings) plus `count`/`filter`. When a sacrifice resolves, submit_decision parks the NEXT opponent from the queue instead of resuming; only when the queue empties does it `resume_or_finalize`. **resume_index is set ONCE** (in apply_trigger_effects, past the sacrifice effect) and untouched across the whole chain â€” the stack item just stays `awaiting_decision` between opponents. **Shared helper `park_edict_sacrifice(session, stack_item, count, filter, queue)`** does build-options-and-park for the first queue candidate that controls an eligible permanent (skips empty boards, tries next), stamping the leftover queue into params; returns the decision id or null if NObody can sac. **Both the initial park (apply_trigger_effects) and every continuation (submit_decision) call it** â€” so `who:'you'` (queue=[controller]) and `who:'opponent'` (queue=[first opponent]) now route through it too with an empty leftover queue (one decision â†’ resume), keeping **SAC1/2/3 behaviour-identical** (verified: 247/247, the prior sacrifice tests still pass after the refactor). whoâ†’queue in apply_trigger_effects: each_opponent = all opponents `order by seat_number`; opponent = first opponent only; you = [controller]. Queue elements are `to_jsonb(player_id::text)`; remaining computed via `jsonb_array_elements ... with ordinality where ord > v_idx+1`. **Zero client change** â€” each opponent's decision is just another `sacrifice` CardPickBody assigned to its `deciding_player_id`; submit_decision has no priority check so the assigned opponent can submit any time. **Harness gained 3-player support:** `Scenario.create(client, numPlayers: 2|3)` (Seat now 'A'|'B'|'C'; C joins only when numPlayers=3, its UUID always exists for typing). Tests ME1 (B then C chain, controller's own creature untouched), ME2 (empty last opponent skipped â†’ resolves), ME3 (empty FIRST opponent skipped on the initial park). Authoring: Zod `who` enum += 'each_opponent', LLM prose (both sacrifice notes). tsc/lint clean. **All sacrifice variants now shipped.**

- [2026-06-05] **Tier-3 X spells (migration 109) â€” variable amount paid as real {X} generic mana, BOTH cast paths.** Scoped via two AskUserQuestion forks: user chose **pay real {X} mana** (not free-pick) AND **both shapes** (targeted Fireball + untargeted Mind Spring). **Core design = resolve X server-side, tied to mana paid:** the card script writes the literal string `amount: "X"` (Zod `AmountSchema = z.union([z.number(), z.literal('X')])`, applied to deal_damage/draw/gain_life/lose_life/mill/add_counters); the client/caller sends a chosen `x_value`; the SERVER charges `x_value` generic mana THEN substitutes it into the effect amount. A client can't pay 1 and deal 999 â€” the damage is whatever mana was paid. **Three seams: (1) `pay_mana_cost` gains `p_x_value` (default 0) and parses `{X}`** â€” the old regex `([0-9]+|[WUBRGC])` silently DROPPED X; new code counts X symbols (`length - length(replace(...,'X',''))`) and adds `x_count * x_value` to generic cost. **Drop+recreate (not a new overload)** so all existing 4-arg callers resolve to the single 5-arg-with-default function (same trick used for cast_spell_effect). **(2) Targeted path (`put_action_on_stack`, mig 105 skeleton reproduced):** reads `(payload->>'x_value')::int`, forwards it to pay_mana_cost; the 4 amount-builders (deal_damage_player/creature, add_counters_creature, draw_cards) resolve amount via new helper `resolve_effect_amount(raw, x)` = `case raw='X' then x else raw::int`. **Signature UNCHANGED â€” X rides in the jsonb payload** (no client RPC-arg churn for the targeted path). **(3) Untargeted path (`cast_spell_effect`, mig 094 reproduced):** gains `p_x_value`, substitutes `"X"`â†’x_value in the top-level effects list (jsonb_agg with `|| jsonb_build_object` merge, so apply_trigger_effects never sees "X"), AND â€” **BEHAVIOR CHANGE** â€” now PAYS the source card's mana cost. The untargeted program path previously paid NOTHING (only put_action_on_stack paid). Guarded by source-from-hand + non-empty mana_cost, so all free-cast fixtures (no mana_cost) are unaffected; treated as in-scope for "pay {X}" (you can't charge the X part without charging the cost). **Minimal client decision deferred to Slice 2:** no mana-color picker needed (engine auto-distributes generic when generic_payment null) â€” the only new client input is a "choose X" number prompt. **Harness needed mana for the first time:** added `Scenario.setMana(seat, pool)` (direct UPDATE) + `manaOf` + `castSpellEffect` xValue passthrough; seed.ts + TestCard type gained `mana_cost` (was never loaded â€” fixtures are all free); fixtures Fireball Test {X}{R} / Mind Spring Test {X}{U}. Tests X1 (Fireballâ†’creature, damage_marked=X, mana charged), X2 (â†’player, life & mana), X3 (insufficient generic rejects), X4 (Mind Spring draws X, charged), X5 (untargeted path also gates on {X}). **244/244, tsc/lint clean.** **Slice 2 (client) SHIPPED:** `getSpellPlan`'s damage/draw/add_counters/spell_effect branches now accept `amount==='X'` (widened the casts to `number | 'X'`) and set `xRequired` (amount 0 placeholder); the 5 cast handlers (dealDamageToPlayer/Creature, addCountersCreature, drawCards, spellEffect) call a new module-level `promptForXValue()` (window.prompt â†’ positive int, abort on cancel) when `xRequired` and pass the result as `xValue`; the 5 actions.ts wrappers gained a trailing `xValue` param that sends `amount:'X' + x_value:N` (server resolves â€” never trusts a client number). **No mana-colour picker** (engine auto-distributes generic). Note: in the client a single-action `draw amount:"X"` (Mind Spring) routes to the `draw` plan â†’ `put_action_on_stack('draw_cards')`, NOT cast_spell_effect â€” so X is exercised through BOTH `put_action_on_stack` (builders + pay_mana_cost) and `cast_spell_effect`; both resolve it. **X spells fully complete end-to-end.** Multi-opponent edict still deferred (user: "xspells first, defer multi after").

- [2026-06-04] **Tier-2 `fight` (migration 101) â€” the first MULTI-target effect.** "Creature you control fights target creature" â€” each deals damage equal to its power to the other, simultaneously (CR 701.12), both can die. **Mechanic = pure reuse, zero new damage/death code:** `apply_fight(session, fighter, fought)` reads BOTH `card_effective_power` (printed + counters + pumps) UP FRONT (so a creature that dies still deals its hit â€” fight is simultaneous), then calls `apply_creature_effect('deal_damage', â€¦)` twice (which marks damage + re-runs the lethal SBA sweep). Fizzles (returns, no damage) if EITHER creature has left the battlefield at resolution. **Cast-path decision: a dedicated `cast_fight` RPC, NOT put_action_on_stack.** Rationale: fight's two-target shape (asymmetric controller roles â€” fighter='you', fought='any') doesn't fit put_action_on_stack's single-target payload, AND a third verbatim reproduction of the ~320-line put_action_on_stack was avoidable. cast_fight is ~110 focused NEW lines modeled on `cast_spell_effect`'s auth/session/turn/priority/timing/source-move skeleton â€” but ADDS `pay_mana_cost` (cast_spell_effect omits it; fight spells should cost mana). Constraint (`game_stack_items_action_type_check`) += `fight_creatures`. - [2026-06-04] **`fight` tail finished (migration 103) â€” deathtouch + generic-mana parity. fight is now COMPLETE.** **(1) Deathtouch.** `move_lethal_damaged_creatures_to_graveyard` already destroys a creature with `dealt_deathtouch_damage=true` AND any marked damage (baseline L4747-4757); combat sets that flag via `card_has_deathtouch`. The gap: `apply_creature_effect`'s `deal_damage` only marked `damage_marked`, never the deathtouch flag â€” so fight (and any non-combat damage) ignored the dealer's deathtouch. Fix: deal_damage now honours an optional `'deathtouch'` boolean param (`dealt_deathtouch_damage = dealt_deathtouch_damage or coalesce((params->>'deathtouch')::boolean,false)` â€” keeps the primitive the single owner of creature mutation, and any future deathtouch-source burn reuses it). `apply_fight` captures BOTH creatures' `card_has_deathtouch` UP FRONT (alongside the powers, since fight is simultaneous â€” a creature that dies still deals its deathtouch hit) and passes the flag per hit. **`card_has_deathtouch` works inside `apply_fight`** despite its `is_session_player(session,auth.uid())` WHERE-guard, because resolve runs with a valid session-player `auth.uid()` (same as combat, which already uses it). **Latent-bug caught (bug-205):** F1/F5/F6 had asserted a 4/4 SURVIVES fighting a Deathtouch Viper (1/1) â€” wrong under CR 702.2 once deathtouch works (1 deathtouch dmg is lethal). Those tests had used the viper as a plain 1/1; swapped them to `Silhana Ledgewalker Test` (1/1, reach, NO deathtouch, NO ETB trigger â€” the go-to "vanilla 1/1 for fight tests"). Added F9 (deathtouch viper kills a 0/4 `Vengeful Wall Test` via 1 lethal dmg, survives since wall has 0 power) + F10 (deathtouch defender kills the 4/4 attacker too). **(2) Generic-mana parity.** Realization: EVERY creature-spell client dispatch already passes `undefined`/null for genericPayment â€” surfacing a generic-mana picker is a SHARED app-wide UI feature, NOT fight-specific. The only fight-specific gap was that `cast_fight` didn't even ACCEPT a generic-payment param (every other cast path threads `generic_payment` jsonb â†’ `pay_mana_cost`). Fix: `cast_fight` gains `p_generic_payment jsonb default null`, forwarded to `pay_mana_cost`. **Signature gotcha:** adding a param changes the function identity, so `create or replace` can't do it â€” must `drop function if exists public.cast_fight(uuid,uuid,uuid,uuid,text)` first, then create the 6-arg version (`...,text,jsonb`); named-param rpc calls that omit `p_generic_payment` still resolve via the default. Client `castFight` wrapper gains `genericPayment?` forwarding (parity; dispatch passes undefined today like the others). **224/224, tsc/lint clean.** **Infra note (not a code bug):** mid-session the local DB started dropping external connections on 54322 ("Connection terminated unexpectedly") while the container reported healthy (33/100 conns, internal psql fine) â€” a Docker hostâ†”container port-forward glitch; fixed by `docker restart supabase_db_LeylineSync` (NOT `supabase start`, which left the DB up and only restarted aux services). **fight is now done end-to-end: engine + spell cast + spell authoring + two-step picker + trigger path + trigger authoring + deathtouch + mana parity.**

- [2026-06-05] **`gain_control` COMPLETED (migration 107) â€” threaten extras + SPELL path; the 104/105 registry's first real payoff.** Two follow-ups from mig 106, both shipped: **(1) Threaten extras.** A real Threaten/Act of Treason also UNTAPS the stolen creature and gives it HASTE (else it's summoning-sick under the new controller and can't attack the turn you take it). gain_control now honours optional `untap`/`haste` booleans: untap clears is_tapped via a `case`-guarded UPDATE clause, haste inserts the same until-EOT 'haste' continuous-effect row grant_keyword uses (always until-EOT even for permanent control â€” haste matters the turn you gain it; next turn it's no longer sick). **(2) SPELL path** (Act of Treason is itself a sorcery, so this is the *canonical* shape, not the trigger). **This is where the 104/105 dispatch registry paid off concretely: NO reproduction of resolve_top_of_stack OR put_action_on_stack.** The whole spell path = (a) `gain_control_creature` added to the game_stack_items action_type CHECK, (b) one new builder `build_stack_payload_gain_control_creature` (creature_simple validation + echo duration/untap/haste), (c) handle_creature_effect reproduced from mig 104 with a one-line change â€” it now injects `acting_controller := p_stack_item.controller_player_id` into the params it passes to apply_creature_effect (mirrors the trigger seam from 106; behavior-neutral for every other creature kind), (d) one `stack_action_handlers` row (handler_fn=handle_creature_effect, builder_fn=the new builder). Contrast with how grant_keyword's spell path (mig 100, PRE-registry) needed verbatim reproduction of the ~320-line put_action_on_stack + resolve_top_of_stack â€” the registry erased that. **Spell path is FULLY harness-tested** (no client needed for verification): `putOnStack('gain_control_creature', {...})` â†’ GC4 (EOT + untap + haste: caster controls, is_tapped=false, haste+control continuous-effect rows present, then expireEffects reverts control to owner and lapses both rows) + GC5 (opponent-only rejects your own creature at cast). **Client wiring** (mirrors grant_keyword mig 100): TargetedCreatureActionType += gain_control_creature, `putGainControlCreatureOnStack` wrapper (carries duration/untap/haste), getSpellPlan detects `gain_control` â†’ a creature_effect plan carrying duration/untap/haste, the creatureEffect dispatch branches on `plan.effect === 'gain_control_creature'`. Authoring now BOTH contexts: registry `['trigger','spell']`, BuilderSpellEffect += gain_control, Zod gained optional untap/haste booleans, LLM prose updated (valid as trigger or instant/sorcery; untap/haste documented). Form models duration+target only; untap/haste are JSON/AI (consistent with not adding a boolean field kind). Added a `Scenario.playerId(seat)` accessor (was private) to assert the caster's id in the spell test. **228/228, tsc/lint clean.** gain_control is now COMPLETE: trigger + spell + threaten extras + authoring in both contexts. **Recipe confirmed: post-registry, adding a creature-targeting SPELL effect = CHECK value + 1 builder + 1 registry row (+ client wrapper/getSpellPlan); the two monster functions are never reproduced.**

- [2026-06-05] **Tier-2 `gain_control` (migration 106) â€” Threaten/Mind Control, TRIGGER path.** "When this enters, gain control of target creature you don't control [until end of turn]." **Key structural difference from every prior creature effect:** control is a DIRECT column (`game_cards.controller_player_id`), NOT a read-through continuous-effect layer like keywords/pump (which the `card_has_*`/`card_effective_power` accessors compute live). So the cleanup sweep â€” which only DELETEs continuous-effect rows â€” can't revert control by deletion. Design: permanent control = a direct UPDATE; until-end-of-turn = the UPDATE **plus** a `'control'` continuous-effect row carrying `{original_controller}`, and `expire_continuous_effects_for_step` gained an explicit RESTORE step (UPDATE controller back from the payload, same expiry predicate as the DELETE, guarded to battlefield-only) that runs BEFORE the delete. **Threading the acting controller:** `apply_creature_effect(session,kind,target,params)` has no controller param; rather than change its signature (and all call sites), `apply_targeted_triggered_ability_effects` now injects `acting_controller := p_controller_id` into the effect params jsonb it passes to apply_creature_effect â€” behavior-NEUTRAL for every other kind (they ignore the extra key). gain_control reads `acting_controller` (raises if absent) + `duration` ('permanent'default|'end_of_turn'). Routed through the creature-target picker by adding 'gain_control' to `trigger_effect_requires_creature_target` (+ target_type creature-only). effect_type CHECK += 'control'. **Reproduced functions** (gain_control is a primitive branch, NOT helped by the 104/105 dispatch registry â€” that was for resolve/put, not apply_creature_effect): apply_creature_effect (from 103), trigger_effect_requires_creature_target + apply_targeted_triggered_ability_effects (from 102), expire_continuous_effects_for_step (from baseline). Authoring: registry entry (duration enum + creatureTargetField, contexts ['trigger']), Zod member + KNOWN_V2, BuilderEffect union (trigger-only, NOT BuilderSpellEffect), LLM prose. Fixtures `Usurp Brute Test` (EOT) + `Dominate Beast Test` (permanent). Tests GC1 (EOT flips then reverts via expireEffects), GC2 (permanent doesn't revert), GC3 (controller restriction). **Test trick (no harness change):** assert control by comparing the taken creature's `controller_player_id` to the SOURCE creature's (= the acting seat) and to its own `owner_id` (= original) â€” both already on `cardState`, so no seatâ†’playerId accessor needed. **226/226, tsc/lint clean.** **Deferred follow-ups:** (1) the "threaten" combat extras â€” untap + grant haste so the stolen creature can actually attack the turn you take it (without haste it's summoning-sick under the new controller); (2) the SPELL/instant path (`gain_control_creature` stack action â€” now CHEAP thanks to the 104/105 registry: a builder row echoing duration + handler_fn handle_creature_effect, but handle_creature_effect would need to inject acting_controller = stack_item.controller_player_id, mirroring the trigger seam). **Recipe note:** an effect that mutates a DIRECT column with an until-EOT duration needs a revert hook in expire_continuous_effects_for_step (the sweep is delete-only); read-through-layer effects (keywords/pump) need nothing there.

- [2026-06-05] **Cast-side dispatch is now DATA-DRIVEN too (migration 105) â€” companion to 104; kills the put_action_on_stack reproduction tax.** `put_action_on_stack` is the cast-side monster re-pasted per creature-targeting SPELL effect (migs 071/079/083/100 each reproduced its ~340 lines to add ONE action type to THREE spots: the whitelist `in(...)`, the per-action validation chain, and the payload-building `case`). 105 extracts each action's **validate-and-build-payload** into a builder of uniform signature `build_stack_payload_*(p_session_id uuid, p_actor uuid, p_payload jsonb, p_timing text, p_target_controller text) returns jsonb` (validates â†’ RAISES on bad input exactly as before â†’ returns the jsonb to store). Reuses the **same `stack_action_handlers` table** via a new nullable `builder_fn` column (null = not castable via put_action_on_stack: cast_permanent/modal_spell/scry/surveil/spell_effect/fight_creatures/triggered_ability use dedicated cast_* RPCs/enqueue). The whitelist `in(...)` is GONE â€” replaced by "the registry has a builder_fn for this action_type" (same 'Unsupported stack action type' error, same early position). The 5 simple creature actions (destroy/bounce/tap/untap/exile) share ONE `build_stack_payload_creature_simple` (identical validation + `{target_card_id,target_controller,timing}` payload). **Ordering-preservation care:** the validation chain originally ran AFTER the sorcery checks and BEFORE mana payment, so the single EXECUTE builder call is placed at that exact spot (raises before any mana paid); the counterspell-instant-timing guard and the sorcery guards STAY inline in the skeleton verbatim (they're action-specific but orthogonal to the reproduction tax, and moving them would change error precedence for malformed input). builder lookup happens early (whitelist position) but the builder CALL happens late (validation position) â€” split to preserve both the early unsupported-type error and the late validation order. counter_spell builder keeps its `for update` lock on the target item (locks persist for the tx regardless of which fn acquires them). Builders SECURITY DEFINER + revoked from public (internal, reached only via skeleton EXECUTE as owner). Pure behavior-preserving (no client/TS change): 224/224 unchanged. **NEW FULL RECIPE â€” a creature-targeting SPELL effect now needs ZERO function reproduction: (1) add the action_type to the game_stack_items CHECK, (2) INSERT/UPDATE a stack_action_handlers row with builder_fn (often the shared creature_simple) + handler_fn (often handle_creature_effect), (3) client wrapper. Both monster dispatchers (resolve + put) are now table-driven.** Remaining per-effect SQL is only genuinely-new mechanics (a new apply_creature_effect kind, or a non-creature_simple payload shape).

- [2026-06-05] **Stack-action dispatch is now DATA-DRIVEN (migration 104) â€” the registry-dispatcher refactor; kills the resolve_top_of_stack reproduction tax.** Every migration 087-103 that added a stack action type had to re-paste the entire ~210-line `resolve_top_of_stack` just to add ONE branch to its `action_type` if/elsif chain (superlinear copy-to-diff cost). 104 removes that: a `stack_action_handlers(action_type pk, handler_fn, description)` lookup table + each old branch lifted VERBATIM into a handler fn of a **uniform signature** `handle_*(p_session_id uuid, p_stack_item public.game_stack_items) returns jsonb`. **Handler contract:** return non-null jsonb â†’ dispatcher returns it DIRECTLY (an awaiting_decision park; item NOT finalized); return null â†’ dispatcher calls `finalize_stack_resolution`. This captures BOTH old branch shapes (side-effect-then-fallthrough-to-finalize = return null; park-for-decision = return the awaiting jsonb). scry/surveil's no-options case returns null (resolver finalizes) â€” same as the old `return finalize_stack_resolution(...)`. The 9 creature-effect action types (deal_damage/pump/destroy/exile/bounce/tap/untap/add_counters/grant_keyword `_creature`) all map to ONE `handle_creature_effect` (it still strips `_creature` â†’ apply_creature_effect kind); scry+surveil share `handle_scry_surveil`. Dispatcher = auth/session-lock/top-item-select (unchanged) then `select handler_fn from stack_action_handlers` + `execute format('select public.%I($1,$2)', v_handler_fn) into v_result using p_session_id, v_stack_item`. **EXECUTE/composite mechanics that worked:** (a) `%I` quotes the table-controlled, public-schema handler name (no injection); the unqualified name is stored and `public.` prepended in the format string (can't `%I` a schema-qualified name â€” it'd quote the dot). (b) the whole `game_stack_items` ROWTYPE var passes fine as a bound `using` param to a composite-typed handler param. **Security:** handlers are SECURITY DEFINER/search_path=public (matching apply_fight et al.), reached ONLY via the dispatcher's EXECUTE which runs as the function owner â€” so NO grant to authenticated, and I `revoke all ... from public` on each (Postgres auto-grants EXECUTE to PUBLIC on creation) so handle_cast_permanent/handle_counter_spell etc. are NOT exposed as raw PostgREST RPCs. **auth.uid() nesting check:** none of the lifted branch bodies read auth.uid() (the single auth check stays in the dispatcher), so definer nesting is behavior-neutral; functions that read it deeper (card_has_deathtouch via apply_fight, apply_trigger_effects) still work because auth.uid() reads a session GUC unaffected by definer nesting. **NEW RECIPE â€” adding a stack action type is now: (1) INSERT one row into stack_action_handlers, (2) create one handle_* fn (+ revoke from public). resolve_top_of_stack is NEVER reproduced again.** Pure behavior-preserving refactor (no client/TS change): 224/224 unchanged, tsc/lint clean. Scoped first slice of the broader dispatch-table idea; `put_action_on_stack` (the OTHER monster that gets re-pasted per creature-targeting SPELL effect) is the next candidate for the same treatment but was left out to keep this diff minimal and verifiable.

- [2026-06-04] **Targeted single-creature effects in the form, via a composite `target` field kind.** Added `destroy`/`exile`/`bounce`/`tap`/`untap`/`pump` as registry entries (contexts trigger+spell). Engine contract confirmed from fixtures (Doom Blade, Banishing Bolt, Banisher Priest, Battlegrowth, Giant Growth): targeted effects use an **inline `target_type` (+ optional `target_controller`) on the action** â€” NOT the `targets[]`/`target_ref` wiring (scripts using target_ref stay JSON-mode; not modeled). New `target` FieldDescriptor kind: stored in-memory as a single option `value` (e.g. `creature_opponent`) but it OWNS two JSON keys â€” `effectToJson` expands it to `target_type`(+`target_controller`), `effectFromJson`/`parseFields` collapse the two keys back by matching options (controller vocab bucketed any/opponent/you via `controllerBucket`; `you`/`controller`/`self`â†’you). Strict-key allow-set special-cases target to permit target_type/target_controller. Combined dropdown chosen over two separate dropdowns (cleaner JSON: omits target_controller when unrestricted, e.g. Doom Blade = `{type:destroy,target_type:creature}`) â€” user picked it. Form UI needed ZERO changes: the existing `FieldControl` select branch renders any field with `options`. **Scope deliberately limited to always-creature-targeted effects.** Deferred: targeted `deal_damage` (Lightning Bolt) and targeted `add_counters` â€” those `type`s already have auto-resolve forms (recipient / on-self) in the registry, so a targeted variant needs a per-type disambiguator (registry is one-entry-per-`type`); a targeted add_counters/deal_damage script correctly stays JSON-mode for now. 121 tests green. This closes the main remaining form capability gap; the dual-shape variant mechanism is the next item if Lightning-Bolt-class cards are wanted in the form.
- [2026-06-04] **Quick-wins pass: spell-context decision effects + empty-field omission + mill.** (1) Enabled `discard`/`may`/`choose_player`/`search_library` as **spell effects** (contexts now `['trigger','spell']`) and added **`mill`** as a new registry entry (`['trigger','spell']`, fields amount+recipient). Verified safe in the engine first: `resolve_top_of_stack` runs `spell_effect` programs through the SAME `apply_trigger_effects` as triggers (migration 094 L552-553), whose `else` branch routes auto-resolve effects (incl. mill) to `apply_targeted_triggered_ability_effects` â€” so any effect that function handles works in both contexts. (2) **Empty-field omission:** optional `text`/`object`/`effect-list` fields that carry no info are now dropped from serialized JSON (`isEmptyValue` helper + skip in `effectToJson`) â€” so a no-filter tutor saves `{search_library,count,to}` not `â€¦filter:{type_line:''}` (fixes the in-game "Search your library for a " prompt; also drops empty `may` prompts). Scalars (number/enum/select) are never "empty" â€” they keep materializing their default (recipientâ†’each_opponent etc.), so step-1 behavior is unchanged. Round-trips stay stable because the in-memory form re-materializes the optional default on parse. - [2026-06-04] **Step 2: four decision effects + recursive field kinds added to the registry.** Added `search_library`, `discard`, `may`, `choose_player` as `EFFECT_REGISTRY` entries (`['trigger']` context only â€” matches the fixtures; spell-context tutors are a one-line add later). Introduced three new `FieldDescriptor` kinds: `text` (free string, e.g. may.prompt), `object` (nested record with its own `fields`, parsed with strict sub-keys â€” for search_library's `filter.type_line`), and `effect-list` (a recursive array of effects parsed in an `itemContext` â€” for may/choose_player's `effects`). `effectDefault`/`effectToJson`/`effectFromJson` now dispatch per kind via mutually-recursive `fieldDefault`/`fieldToJson`/`parseFieldValue`+`parseFields` helpers; the form renderer gained `text`/`object` branches in `FieldControl` plus a recursive `EffectListControl` that reuses a now-generic `EffectEditor(context)` (so nested rows recurse back through `EffectFields`). Optional-default materialization is consistent with step 1 (a tutor without `filter`/`to` round-trips with the defaults filled). `effect-list` is always required (absent `effects` â†’ JSON mode). The AI guide picked the four up automatically (it derives from `BUILDER_EFFECT_TYPES`). 92 characterization tests green (was 82), tsc+lint clean. Chose to build the `object`/`effect-list` primitives properly rather than special-case the filter, because they're reusable for the still-growing vocabulary (the whole point of step 1).
- [2026-06-04] **Card-behavior guided form becomes registry-driven (the engine vocabulary will grow a lot).** Replaced the per-effect hand-coded switches (`defaultEffect`, `effectToJson`, `parseEffects`, `parseSpellEffect`) and per-type form JSX with one declarative `EFFECT_REGISTRY` (`lib/game/card-behavior-registry.ts`): each effect type declares `{type,label,contexts,fields}` once, and defaults / JSON serialize / strict JSON parse / form widgets all derive from it. Form rendering is now a generic `<EffectFields>`/`<FieldControl>` walk over `fields` (number/enum/select kinds). `BUILDER_EFFECT_TYPES`/`BUILDER_SPELL_EFFECT_TYPES`/`BUILDER_RECIPIENTS`/`BUILDER_TOKEN_NAMES` are re-exported from the registry so the AI guide (`card-behavior-llm.ts`) stays in sync from the same source. **Deliberately NOT done:** generate the form from the Zod schema (schema is a loose validation contract, not a UI spec â€” kept as a separate source: schema = "is it valid", registry = "how to edit/teach"); couple schema to registry; or fold activated abilities into the registry (different cost+effect shape, left hand-coded). Adding a new form-editable effect = one registry entry (+ migration + Zod entry). Step 1 of 2: this is a pure refactor reproducing current capability; step 2 adds search_library/discard/may/choose_player (needs a recursive `effect-list` field for the nested ones). Chosen over (a) freezing the form and leaning on AI/JSON forever, and (b) a read-only structured preview â€” because the user confirmed the vocabulary keeps growing, so only schema-from-one-source scales.
- [2026-06-04] **Unified the form parser to STRICT (was asymmetric).** Found the two JSONâ†’form parsers disagreed: `parseSpellEffect` was strict (unknown key / missing field â†’ JSON mode) but `parseEffects` (trigger effects) was lenient â€” it ignored unknown keys (silently dropping them on save) and defaulted a missing `amount` to 0. The registry needs one rule, so unified to strict for both contexts: unknown key, missing required field, or invalid enum value â†’ JSON mode; optional fields (recipientâ†’each_opponent, create_token.countâ†’1) keep defaults. Behavior change: a few malformed-but-previously-lenient trigger scripts now open in JSON instead of Form (no more silent data loss). Locked by characterization tests (`tests/unit/card-behavior-builder.test.ts`) written BEFORE the refactor â€” 82 cases pinning the form/JSON classification, form round-trip stability, and default-factory shapes. Chosen over faithfully reproducing the asymmetry (would bake latent bugs into the clean registry). User approved.
- [2026-06-02] **Local bootstrap split out of the push path (so `supabase db push` is safe for hosted).** The squash baseline + local-only relax-FK migration were moved OUT of `supabase/migrations/` into `supabase/local-bootstrap/` (`00_baseline.sql`, `01_relax_fks.sql`). `supabase/migrations/` now holds ONLY the real incrementals (087+) â€” that folder is the `db push` payload, and the bootstrap must never be in it (baseline would collide with the existing hosted schema; relax-FK would drop prod FKs). Consequence: `supabase db reset`/`migration up` can no longer build local (the incrementals assume base tables exist) â€” local is rebuilt by **`npm run test:db:setup`** (`scripts/setup-local-test-db.mjs`: drops `public`, applies bootstrap then migrations via a direct `pg` connection). Hosted deploy = `supabase link` + `supabase db push` (use `supabase migration list` to see the diff; `migration repair --status applied <ver>` to mark 087/088 done if already hand-applied). Chosen over Option B (reconcile-only via repair, leaves relax-FK a footgun in the push path) and Option A (keep pasting SQL manually). Replaces the earlier note that the relax-FK lived at `supabase/migrations/00000000000001_local_test_relax_fks.sql` â€” that path no longer exists.
- [2026-06-02] **Local DB = squashed dump baseline, not migration replay.** Discovered the incremental migration chain is not replayable from scratch (base tables cards/game_cards/game_players/profiles created out-of-band on hosted â†’ bug-104; AND multiple returns-table functions change shape via create-or-replace â†’ 42P13; AND Supabase's leading-version-digit keying makes mid-chain drop-shims impossible). Since hosted is applied MANUALLY (migrations/ isn't the prod driver), chose to squash for local: `supabase/migrations/` = one full-schema dump baseline + a local-only relax-FK migration; the 88 incrementals archived in `supabase/migrations_archive/` as history. New migrations still go in migrations/ and get pasted to hosted manually as before. Rejected: surgical per-table baseline (chain still didn't replay), drop-shim injection (version-PK collisions), out-of-band load (bespoke, db reset wouldn't work).
- [2026-06-02] **Test chamber = programmatic harness first (Option A), against local Supabase.** Chose a code-driven regression suite (drives real RPCs, asserts state) over an interactive in-app sandbox (Option B) as the first build â€” higher leverage (CI-able, protects the 084â€“086 refactors, encodes docs/test-plan-079-086.md permanently), and its scenario helpers (`place`/`cast`/`resolveStack`/`snapshot`) are the foundation a sandbox would later reuse, so it isn't throwaway. DB target: **local Supabase via Docker** over bare-Postgres-with-auth-shims or a hosted test project â€” the project is already supabase-initialized (config.toml) and Docker is installed; full prod fidelity (`db reset` replays the exact migrations), fast, offline. Cost accepted: tests need Docker Desktop running. Implementation keystone: direct `pg` + `request.jwt.claims` to satisfy `auth.uid()` (see Key Learnings).
